```
Nick & Carol:

Please check with Bob England of England Technical Services, but I'm
almost positive that COBOL RPC from ETS can help you accomplish
exactly what you need to do.  COBOL RPC provides a server daemon which
can launch an instance of a server-based COBOL application.  It then
provides the ability to pass a parameter block across TCP/IP.  The
parameter block can be passed from a client machine to a server, vice
versa or from one server to another.

ETS also has versions which work identically on UNIX servers or
Windows NT servers.  I carbon copied Bob on this e-mail so that he is
aware of your interest.

The nice thing about COBOL RPC is that everything is done directly
from your COBOL program.  The other nice thing about ETS is that Bob
England is a great guy, an amazing technician and very easy to work
with.

(Ok, Bob...now that I said such wonderful things, do I get a free
Mercedes Benz from ETS or do I just qualify for a Christmas card from
ETS this year?)    ;-)

Good luck!


Bob Wolfe, flexus
Check out The Flexus COBOL Page at http://www.flexus.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Sockets and Daemons

- **From:** Albert Ratzlaff <albert@infonet.com.py>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35EAF695.1FD1329B@infonet.com.py>`
- **References:** `<35eab473.1278121@news.demon.co.uk>`

```


Nick & Carol Lucas-White wrote:

> Does anyone know of a daemon (hopefully freeware)  that can be set to
> "monitor" a particular port number specified in /etc/services that can
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> appreciated. Thanks.

This is very basic, but there you go:

#include <stdio.h>
#include <sys/types.h>
#include <sys/socket.h>
#include <netdb.h>
#include <netinet/in.h>

#ifdef DEBUG
#define D(x) fprintf(stderr, x);
#else
#define D(x)
#endif

void doit(int);
void err_sys(char *);
int writen(int, char *, int);
int readn(int, char *, int);
int readline(int, char *, int);
char *myservice = "cpcsrvd";

main(argc, argv)
int argc;
char *argv[];
{
    int sockfd, newsockfd;
    int child_pid;
    struct servent *myservent;
    struct sockaddr_in srv_addr;
    short srv_port;
    struct sockaddr_in cli_addr;
    short cli_port;
    int cli_len;

    D("myservent")
    myservent = getservbyname(myservice, "tcp");
    if (myservent == NULL)
 err_sys("getservbyname error");
    if ((srv_port = ntohs(myservent->s_port)) == 0)
 err_sys("port error");
    D("socket")
    if ((sockfd = socket(AF_INET, SOCK_STREAM, 0)) < 0)
 err_sys("socket error");
    bzero((char *)&srv_addr, sizeof(srv_addr));
    srv_addr.sin_family = AF_INET;
    srv_addr.sin_addr.s_addr = htonl(INADDR_ANY);
    srv_addr.sin_port = htons(srv_port);
    D("bind")
    if (bind(sockfd, (struct sockaddr *)&srv_addr, sizeof(srv_addr))  < 0)

 err_sys("bind error");
    D("listen")
    if (listen(sockfd, 5) < 0)
 err_sys("listen error");

    for (;;) {
 cli_len = sizeof(cli_addr);
 D("accept")
 newsockfd = accept(sockfd, (struct sockaddr *)&cli_addr, &cli_len);
      /* blocks */
 if (newsockfd < 0)
     err_sys("accept error");
 D("fork")
 if ((child_pid = fork()) < 0)
     err_sys("fork error");
 else if (child_pid == 0) {
     close(sockfd);   /* child */
     doit(newsockfd);   /* process the request */
     /* NOT REACHED */
 }
 D("parent")
 close(newsockfd);   /* parent */
    }
}

void err_sys(s)
char *s;
{
    fprintf(stderr, "cpcsrvd: %s\n", s);
    perror("cpcsrvd");
    exit(1);
}

#define MAXARGV 20
void doit(sockfd)
int sockfd;
{
    char *av[MAXARGV+1];
    char cobol[BUFSIZ+1];
    int n;

    D("doit")
    if ((n = recv(sockfd, cobol, BUFSIZ, 0)) < 1)
 err_sys("recv error");
/* first message we receive is name of cobol object file to execute */
/* this works for RM/COBOL, you'd have to adapt it to other COBOLs */
/* after invocation, the COBOL program has an open connection on file
descriptor 0 */
    cobol[n] = '\0';
    av[0] = "runcobol";
    av[1] = cobol;
    av[2] = "-k";
    av[3] = NULL;
    if (dup2(sockfd, 0) < 0)
 err_sys("dup2 error");
    close(sockfd);
    if (execv("/usr/bin/runcobol", av) < 1)
 err_sys("execv error");
    exit(1);
}

int writen(fd, ptr, nbytes)
register int fd;
register char *ptr;
register int nbytes;
{
    int nleft;
    int nwritten;

    nleft = nbytes;
    while (nleft > 0) {
 nwritten = write(fd, ptr, nleft);
 if (nwritten < 0)   /* error */
     return(nwritten);
 nleft -= nwritten;
 ptr += nwritten;
    }
    return(nbytes - nleft);
}

int readn(fd, ptr, nbytes)
register int fd;
register char *ptr;
register int nbytes;
{
    int nleft;
    int nread;

    nleft = nbytes;
    while (nleft > 0) {
 nread = read(fd, ptr, nleft);
 if (nread < 0)
     return(nread);   /* error */
 else if (nread == 0)
     break;    /* EOF */
 nleft -= nread;
 ptr += nread;
    }
    return(nbytes - nleft);
}

int readline(fd, ptr, maxlen)
register int fd;
register char *ptr;
register int maxlen;
{
    int n;
    int rc;
    char c;

    for (n = 1; n < maxlen; n++) {
 if ((rc = read(fd, &c, 1)) == 1) {
     *ptr++ = c;
     if (c == '\n')
  break;
 } else if (rc == 0) {
     if (n == 1)
  return(0); /* EOF, no data read */
     else
  break;  /* EOF, some data was read */
 } else
     return(-1);  /* error */
    }

    *ptr = 0;
    return(n);
}


Most of it copied from various sources.

Regards
Albert Ratzlaff
```

#### ↳ Re: Sockets and Daemons

- **From:** pitchl@tdbank.ca (Lew Pitcher)


#### ↳ Re: IBM mainframe COBOL - how to close an output file and reopen it with a different DSN

- **From:** zberger@ldl.net
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6sf16g$848$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`
- **References:** `<6s0p5r$4v0$1@holly.prod.itd.earthlink.net> <6s7dfq$31b$1@ash.prod.itd.earthlink.net> <6s9f25$cin@dfw-ixnews10.ix.netcom.com> <35ea94fc.773118@news.pnc.com.au> <35EAB5A5.8C8D3914@zip.com.au>`

```
Ok, this is from memory so don't beat me up when the names don't line up
perfectly:

01 MY-FILE-NAME.
  05 PIC X(??)VALUE 'MYDSN.XX'.
  05 MFN-9 999 VALUE 001.
  05 PIC X(??) VALUE 'WHATEVER'.
...
CALL 'COBDYNAL' USING MY-FILE-NAME
...
CSECT COBDYNAL
  SHOP_STANDARD_ENTRY_MACRO,ENTRY=MAIN
*
MYDDNAMA ACB ** YOUR ACB OR DCB HERE **
MYDDNAMR RPL ** YOUR RPL IF NEEDED **
MYDDNAMX EXLST ** YOUR EXLST IF NEEDED **
*
S99ARA DS CL500
AL_DDNAME DC   AL2(DALDDNAM)
  DC    X'0001'
  DC    X'0008'
  DC    CL8'MYDDNAME'
AL_DSNNAME DC  AL2(DALDSNAM)
  DC    X'0001'
ALDSNLL  DC    X'002C'
ALDSN    DC    CL44'MYDSN.XX001.WHATEVER'
AL_STAT   DC   AL2(DALSTATS)
  DC    X'0001'
  DC    X'0001'
  DC    X'08' SHR
  IEFZB4D0
  IEFZB4D2
S99ERBLN EQU   (S99RBEND-S99RB)
MAIN  EQU *
  XR    R15,R15
  USING S99RBP,R1
  LA    R14,S99RBPTR+4
  USING S99RB,R14
  ST    R14,S99RBPTR
  OI    S99RBPTR,S99RBPND
  XC    S99RB(S99ERBLN),S99RB
  MVI   S99RBLN,S99ERBLN
  MVI   S99VERB,S99VRBUN
  LA    R15,S99RB+S99ERBLN
  USING S99TUPL,R15
  ST    R15,S99TXTPP
  LA    R2,AL_DDNAME
  ST    R2,S99TUPTR
  LA    R15,4(R15)
  OI    S99TUPTR,S99TUPLN
  DYNALLOC
  LR    R1,0(R1)
  MVC   ALDSN,0(44,R1)
  XR    R15,R15
  LA    R1,AL_AREA
  XC    0(256,R1),0(R1)
  XC    0(L'AL_AREA-256,R1),256(R1)
  USING S99RBP,R1
  LA    R14,S99RBPTR+4
  USING S99RB,R14
  ST    R14,S99RBPTR
  OI    S99RBPTR,S99RBPND
  XC    S99RB(S99ERBLN),S99RB
  MVI   S99RBLN,S99ERBLN
  MVI   S99VERB,S99VRBAL
  LA    R15,S99RB+S99ERBLN
  XR    R15,R15
  USING S99TUPL,R15
  ST    R15,S99TXTPP
  LA    R2,AL_DDNAME
  ST    R2,S99TUPTR
  LA    R15,4(R15)
  LA    R2,AL_DSNNAME
  ST    R2,S99TUPTR
  LA    R15,4(R15)
  LA    R2,AL_STAT
  ST    R2,S99TUPTR
  LA    R15,4(R15)
  OI    S99TUPTR,S99TUPLN
  DYNALLOC
  SHOP_STANDARD_EXIT_ROUTINE
  END   COBDYNAL

In article <35EAB5A5.8C8D3914@zip.com.au>,
  Ken Foskey <waratah@zip.com.au> wrote:
> This is from the proposed standard and not in the currect MVS release.
>
…[39 more quoted lines elided]…
>

http://www.dejanews.com/rg_mkgrp.xp   Create Your Own Free Member Forum
```

```
Ok, this is from memory so don't beat me up when the names don't line up
perfectly:

01 MY-FILE-NAME.
  05 PIC X(??)VALUE 'MYDSN.XX'.
  05 MFN-9 999 VALUE 001.
  05 PIC X(??) VALUE 'WHATEVER'.
...
ADD +1 TO MFN-9
CALL 'COBDYNAL' USING MY-FILE-NAME
...
CSECT COBDYNAL
  SHOP_STANDARD_ENTRY_MACRO,ENTRY=MAIN
*
MYDDNAMA ACB ** YOUR ACB OR DCB HERE **
MYDDNAMR RPL ** YOUR RPL IF NEEDED **
MYDDNAMX EXLST ** YOUR EXLST IF NEEDED **
*
S99ARA DS CL500
```

- **Message-ID:** `<35eafdc6.26842831@news.enter.net>`

```
paulr@bix.com (paulr) wrote:

>#include <stdio.h>
>main() {
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
>: C++.  Any leads appreciated. 

Paul:

BRAVO!

In reality, you may have written the most reliable solution for
writing an application in COBOL and running (or at leas launching) it
from a C++ application.

From what I have observed, there really isn't a great solution for
successful automated translation of COBOL to C or C++ unless, of
course, your application is the highly complex and well-known, "Hello
World" application.


Bob Wolfe, flexus
Check out The Flexus COBOL Page at http://www.flexus.com
```

## Thread: IBM mainframe COBOL - how to close an output file and reopen it with a different DSN — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe) · [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Re: IBM mainframe COBOL - how to close an output file and reopen it with a different DSN

- **From:** "Paul M. Dorfman" <pdorfma@ucs.att.com>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35EAFB75.246B9A0F@ucs.att.com>`
- **References:** `<6s0p5r$4v0$1@holly.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`

```
Jim Gallagher wrote:
> 
> Hello,
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> Jim Gallagher
 
Jim,

In this (COBOL) shop such programs are usually written in SAS and built in the
job stream as a separate JCL step. For data driven i/o names, SAS is just the
right tool for the job. We have never had any problem with this solution.
However, it depends on the shop: it may not have SAS installed, SOPs may
prohibit its use in production, or SAS expertise may not be readily
available.     

Paul
```

#### ↳ Re: Cobol editor

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc123@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<D5BG1.62$eZ3.143278@news3.mia.bellsouth.net>`
- **References:** `<35EACCC8.14B5@popd.ix.netcom.com>`

```
Don Tarshes wrote:
>Does anyone know of a good cobol editor, PD or otherwise?  One sensitive
>to reserved words, correct column positions, etc.?  Thanks for the help.


For programmers, editors can be a subject of passion rivaling that for
their loved ones. ;-)   But a good, relatively inexpensive editor is
Multi-Edit.  You can buy it on the web pretty cheap ($129 US).  My only
gripe is that you *cannot* get a printed manual, and there is no complete
manuel, even for download.  The online help is good though, and Multi-Edit
is very powerful and flexible.  You can also download the 97 page book
that comes with the retail version as a PDF file.
```

- **From:** housej5@gate.net

- **Message-ID:** `<35EB4704.5CE4AB51@gate.net>`

```
Hello All,
  I have just graduated from USF with a certificate in Cobol
Programming. We did all our programming on a IBM Mainframe. We learned
TSO/ISPF, MVS/JCL, Cobol, and Cobol II, and finally some VSAM , and DB2
stuff. We didn't do much of the VSAM and DB2 , but enough to get started
in it. Since  a lot of you have written many resumes, I was wondering if
any of you experienced programmers could look at my resume for me and
give me some advice. My first one was real basic, but I had a lady from
a consulting firm tell me to explain a little more what I had done since
I didn't have any experience. If you have the time to check out my
resume, just reply this message back to me and I will send you my
resume. Any advice you can give me before I go to one of these job fairs

  Thanks !
       Jeff H.
```

## Thread: zero totals — 1 this month / 2 total

### Re: zero totals

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** alt.cobol,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6sfmv6$1oa@sjx-ixn5.ix.netcom.com>`
- **References:** `<35EB4B2C.3257@swbell.net>`

```
I haven't studied the attached code yet - but this person clearly identified
that they are doing homework AND they showed their work.  Can someone help?

Nick -
    This type of question may do better in the comp.lang.cobol newsgroup
than in the alt.cobol newsgroup - so I am CC'ing it.

P.S.  This type of program is why I still LOVE the Report-Writer module (but
understand that it is rarely taught at this stage of formal training).  In
RW, all you would need is a single declarative with a USE BEFORE REPORTING
and then use the SUPPRESS verb.


Nick Woroniak wrote in message <35EB4B2C.3257@swbell.net>...
>I'm a student who is racking his brains trying to suppres zero totals on
>a multi-level control break program.

>           ADD +1 TO WS-PAYROLL-RPT-LINE-COUNT.
```

<a id="t-a912abd813"></a>
## Thread: 'Cutesie-Poo' Programmer's Tricks — 1 msgs

### Re: 'Cutesie-Poo' Programmer's Tricks

- **From:** mark0young@aol.com (Mark0Young)
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1998083103515400.XAA26661@ladder03.news.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<35DEA699.63F9BFA9@hankel.mersinet.co.uk>`

```
In article <35DEA699.63F9BFA9@hankel.mersinet.co.uk>, Charles F Hankel
<charles@hankel.mersinet.co.uk> writes:

>> ported program was amended and recompiled on the new 370, the new MVCL
>> was generated, which abended like bombs when overlapping.
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>

The nature of the MVCL is that it will set a condition code (NOT an abend, just
a condition code that can be tested with a BC or BCR) and does not do any
moving of data if the sending area and receiving area overlap.

This bug can still bite programmers in CICS if they are dealing with varying
lengths of DFHCOMMAREA and always attempt to move the largest one.

It is impossible for the operating system to anticipate this because we are
talking of a move instruction (MVCL = MoVe Character Long), not something that
the operating system will intercept, and the condition set is just one of the
routine condition codes that many arithmatic functions normally set.

In the DOS/VS COBOL manual, it stated that if one is moving more than 768 bytes
(what three MVCs can move), it would generate a MVCL unless operands
overlapped. (Overlapping operands would cause a subroutine call to be
generated.)

Mark A. Young
```

<a id="t-e8865e0c6e"></a>
## Thread: BASIC to COBOL — 2 msgs

### BASIC to COBOL

- **From:** Rick Ritchie <monsters@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<35EA9976.70B872E3@ix.netcom.com>`

```
Thanks All for your Help last week on the translation of the Basic
program to COBOL. I have another question that I could use your Help
with. Can anyone tell me how to execute a COBOL (MF 3.0) program from a
DOS based BASIC program. The other way would be fine also but I keep
getting "memory arena error" when I call (or chain) from a cobol program
even though I used MODEL"SMALL". All of these programs run in a DOS
environment (where have I seen that word before??). Anyway your help
would be greatly appreciated.
```

#### ↳ Re: BASIC to COBOL

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@aiservices.com>
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<XbyG1.1140$Kt4.5717431@news1.atlantic.net>`
- **References:** `<35EA9976.70B872E3@ix.netcom.com>`

```

Rick Ritchie wrote in message <35EA9976.70B872E3@ix.netcom.com>...
>Thanks All for your Help last week on the translation of the Basic
>program to COBOL. I have another question that I could use your Help
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>
You load and execute a COBOL (.EXE) program from BASIC by using the
SHELL command.

You load and execute a BASIC (.EXE) program from (MF) COBOL by using
CALL X"91" function 35.

It is not possible to call or chain to a BASIC program from (MF) COBOL.

It may be possible to call (not chain) a (MF) COBOL (.OBJ) from BASIC
but it depends upon the BASIC. See the (MF) COBOL User Guide for
information on "Interfacing and Mixed-Language Programming."
-------------------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >
```

---

## Thread: Thanks for your responses to my Posting Question. — 1 msgs

### Thanks for your responses to my Posting Question.

- **From:** mrigsby@magicorp.com
- **Date:** 1998-08-31T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,comp.databases.ibm-db,comp.lang.c++,comp.soft-sys.sas
- **Message-ID:** `<6se8ah$7kp$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com>`

```
I know most of you out there really don't care about the question that I
asked last week but a good number of you  did answer my question.  The
majority of the responses I received said that it was fine to post jobs to
these news groups, on the condition that I am courteous and conscience of
others feelings.  So here is what I will do.

1.)  I will only post once a week to each news group. 2.) I will include
multiple jobs in each posting. 3.) Salary location and requirements will be
included. 4.) I will place the title "Job Opening" in the subject line, this
way anyone who is  not currently looking for a job can ignore the message,
and newsgroup  robots will not pick it up.

  I hope that this is satisfactory for all and I hope you have a great day. 
Thank you once again for your responses.



-----== Posted via Deja News, The Leader in Internet Discussion ==-----
http://www.dejanews.com/rg_mkgrp.xp   Create Your Own Free Member Forum
```
